    112 +      "Stop")

    118 +          if [ -n "$TRANSCRIPT_PATH" ] && [ -f "$TRANSCRIPT_PATH" ]; then
    119 +              debug_log "Reading transcript from: $TRANSCRIPT_PATH"
    120 +  
    121 +              # Get the last assistant message from the transcript
    122 +              LAST_RESPONSE=$(tail -20 "$TRANSCRIPT_PATH" | grep '"role":"assistant"' | tail -1 | sed 's/.*"content":"//' |

    123 +  
    124 +              if [ -n "$LAST_RESPONSE" ]; then
    125 +                  debug_log "Found assistant response in transcript"

    127 +                  append_to_session "⏺ $LAST_RESPONSE"

    129 +              fi
    130 +          fi
    131 +          ;;
    132 +  
    133        "SessionEnd")

⏺ Read(/Users/oliver/Library/Mobile Documents/com~apple~CloudDocs/dev/webaps/labcastarr/.env.production)


✻ Thinking…

  The .env.production file contains the correct value! But somehow it's still showing localhost.
  Wait, I think I understand the issue now. Let me check if there's another `.env` file in the project root (not in the frontend directory) that might be overriding this:

⏺ List all environment files in the project root
⎿  -rw-------@ 1 oliver  staff  1705 Sep 19 20:38 /Users/oliver/Library/Mobile Documents/com~apple~CloudDocs/dev/webaps/labcastarr/.env
⎿  -rw-------@ 1 oliver  staff  1587 Sep 13 13:25 /Users/oliver/Library/Mobile Documents/com~apple~CloudDocs/dev/webaps/labcastarr/.env.backup
⎿  -rw-r--r--@ 1 oliver  staff  2098 Sep 17 16:55 /Users/oliver/Library/Mobile Documents/com~apple~CloudDocs/dev/webaps/labcastarr/.env.example
⎿  -rw-r--r--@ 1 oliver  staff    90 Sep 13 13:25 /Users/oliver/Library/Mobile Documents/com~apple~CloudDocs/dev/webaps/labcastarr/.env.minimal
⎿  -rw-r--r--@ 1 oliver  staff  1748 Sep 20 12:53 /Users/oliver/Library/Mobile Documents/com~apple~CloudDocs/dev/webaps/labcastarr/.env.production


✻ Thinking…

  Aha! There's a `.env` file in the project root! Docker Compose loads `.env` by default if no `env_file` is specified, and it might have precedence over or be loaded in addition to the .env.production file. Let me check what's in that file:

⏺ Read(/Users/oliver/Library/Mobile Documents/com~apple~CloudDocs/dev/webaps/labcastarr/.env)


Found the issue! The root `.env` file contains `NEXT_PUBLIC_API_URL=http://localhost:8000` which is overriding our production values. Docker Compose loads the default `.env` file before the `env_file: .env.production`, causing the localhost value to take precedence.

Let me fix this by commenting out the conflicting environment variable in the root `.env` file:

⏺ Edit(/Users/oliver/Library/Mobile Documents/com~apple~CloudDocs/dev/webaps/labcastarr/.env)

Perfect! I found the issue. The error is: `passlib.exc.UnknownHashError: hash could not be identified`

The problem is that the existing user's password hash in the database was created with the old SHA-256 method from the domain entity, but our new authentication system is trying to use bcrypt through passlib. The two systems are incompatible.

I need to update the authentication system to handle this gracefully. Let me create a hybrid approach that can handle both hash types during the transition period:

## Deep Analysis: JWT Verification Issue Root Cause

After thorough investigation, I've identified the **exact root cause** of the JWT verification failure in production Docker environment.

### The Problem
JWT tokens are created successfully but immediately fail verification with "Invalid or expired token", affecting both `/v1/auth/me` and `/v1/auth/validate-token` endpoints. This works in local development but fails consistently in Docker production.

### Root Cause: Module Import Order & Global Instance Timing

**The Issue**: The JWT service is instantiated as a global variable at module import time, but it reads configuration values that might not be fully loaded yet.

**Critical Code Locations:**
1. **`jwt.py:245`**: `jwt_service = JWTService()` (global instance created at import)
2. **`jwt.py:9`**: `from app.core.config import settings` (triggers settings instantiation)
3. **`jwt.py:42-46`**: `JWTService.__init__()` reads `settings.jwt_secret_key` at creation time
4. **`config.py:135`**: `settings = Settings()` (global settings instance)

**The Timing Problem:**
- When `jwt.py` is imported, it immediately creates the global `jwt_service` instance
- This instance reads `settings.jwt_secret_key` at that moment
- If environment variables aren't fully loaded when the module imports, it uses the default value: `"your-secret-key-change-in-production"`
- In Docker production, environment loading timing differs from local development

**Why Tokens Fail:**
- JWT service might be initialized with default secret key instead of production secret
- Token creation and verification both use the same misconfigured instance
- Even though environment variables are correctly set in the container, the JWT service was already instantiated with defaults

### Evidence Supporting This Theory:
1. ✅ Login endpoint works (creates tokens)
2. ❌ Verification immediately fails (same JWT service instance)
3. ✅ Environment variables are correct in container (`JWT_SECRET_KEY=your-jwt-secret-key-change-in-production-2024`)
4. ✅ JWT payload decodes correctly when manually parsed
5. ✅ Issue only occurs in Docker production, not local development

You're absolutely right - we're running in circles. Let me clearly identify what's actually happening:

## The Core Issue

The JWT authentication is failing at the **token verification step**. Here's what's working and what's not:

**✅ Working:**
- Login endpoint returns valid JWT tokens
- JWT service initialization shows correct configuration
- Token creation is successful

**❌ Failing:**
- Token verification immediately returns "Invalid or expired token"
- Both `/v1/auth/me` and `/v1/auth/validate-token` endpoints fail

## The Actual Test That's Failing

Let me decode a fresh token to see what's inside:

⏺ Analyze the JWT token structure and timing

Perfect! Now I can see the exact issue:

## The Real Problem

The token is **valid, not expired, and has correct structure**. The issue is in the **JWT signature verification process**.

**The token creation and verification are using different secret keys or algorithms.**

Let me verify this by checking if there are multiple JWT service instances being created with different configurations:

⏺ Read(/Users/oliver/Library/Mobile Documents/com~apple~CloudDocs/dev/webaps/labcastarr/backend/app/core/jwt.py)


## Root Cause Identified!

The issue is **multiple JWT service instances being created with different secret keys**. Here's what's happening:

1. **Token Creation** (login endpoint): Uses one JWT service instance with secret key A
2. **Token Verification** (auth middleware): Uses a different JWT service instance with secret key B

Even though we implemented lazy initialization, the issue is that **each endpoint is calling `get_jwt_service()` separately, potentially creating different instances if the settings change between calls**.

⏺ ExitPlanMode()


## Root Cause Identified!

The issue is **multiple JWT service instances being created with different secret keys**. Here's what's happening:

1. **Token Creation** (login endpoint): Uses one JWT service instance with secret key A
2. **Token Verification** (auth middleware): Uses a different JWT service instance with secret key B

Even though we implemented lazy initialization, the issue is that **each endpoint is calling `get_jwt_service()` separately, potentially creating different instances if the settings change between calls**.

⏺ TodoWrite()

⏺ Edit(/Users/oliver/Library/Mobile Documents/com~apple~CloudDocs/dev/webaps/labcastarr/backend/app/core/jwt.py)

Perfect! I found the actual issue. The error shows `passlib.exc.UnknownHashError: hash could not be identified` in `auth.py:64`. The password verification is failing because the existing user has a hash format that passlib cannot identify. Let me check the current user data in the database:

⏺ Check current user password hash format
⎿  1|Oliver Barreto|oliver@oliverbarreto.com|3090cc4aa5e1f54b05dc95b2f654aad0b2cc44dc309c1baef779c20527898e8a


Now I see the exact issue! The password hash `3090cc4aa5e1f54b05dc95b2f654aad0b2cc44dc309c1baef779c20527898e8a` is a SHA-256 hash (64 characters), but the `verify_password` function in `jwt.py:189` is calling `pwd_context.verify()` directly which only handles bcrypt. The fallback to `_verify_legacy_password` is only triggered if bcrypt verification throws an exception, but passlib is throwing `UnknownHashError` before that.

Let me fix the `verify_password` function to handle this properly:

⏺ TodoWrite()

Excellent! I found the root cause! The error `Manual jose decode FAILED: Subject must be a string.` reveals the issue. The JWT library expects the `sub` (subject) claim to be a string, but I'm passing an integer (`1`).

This is a classic JWT specification requirement - the `sub` claim must be a string. Let me fix this in the JWT service:
